[24/11/24, 11:39:16 PM] Shammi MPSTME: ### **NoSQL Databases: A Comprehensive Guide**

NoSQL databases are a class of database management systems that provide a mechanism for storing, retrieving, and managing data in formats other than traditional relational databases. They are designed to handle unstructured, semi-structured, and structured data with flexibility and scalability.

---

### **Key Characteristics of NoSQL Databases**
1. **Schema Flexibility:**
   - No predefined schema; data can be added without defining structure beforehand.
   
2. **Scalability:**
   - Horizontally scalable, meaning you can add more servers to handle increased load.

3. **High Performance:**
   - Optimized for fast data retrieval and high-throughput operations.

4. **Distributed Architecture:**
   - Data is often distributed across multiple nodes, ensuring fault tolerance and availability.

5. **Support for Diverse Data Models:**
   - Designed for use cases that relational databases struggle with, such as hierarchical or graph-based relationships.

---

### **Types of NoSQL Databases**

1. **Document Databases:**
   - Store data in JSON, BSON, or XML documents.
   - Each document is self-contained and can include nested structures.
   - Example: **MongoDB, Couchbase**
   - Use Case: Content management systems, user profiles, catalog data.

   **Example Document:**
   ```json
   {
       "user_id": 1,
       "name": "Alice",
       "orders": [
           { "order_id": 101, "item": "Laptop", "price": 1500 },
           { "order_id": 102, "item": "Phone", "price": 800 }
       ]
   }
   ```

---

2. **Key-Value Stores:**
   - Data is stored as key-value pairs, similar to a dictionary.
   - Very fast for simple lookups and is highly scalable.
   - Example: **Redis, DynamoDB**
   - Use Case: Session management, caching, real-time data.

   **Example Key-Value Pair:**
   ```
   Key: "user_1"
   Value: { "name": "Alice", "age": 30 }
   ```

---

3. **Column-Family Stores:**
   - Store data in a columnar format, where each row is organized into columns grouped in families.
   - Example: **Apache Cassandra, HBase**
   - Use Case: Time-series data, logs, analytics.

   **Example:**
   ```
   RowKey: 1
   Column Family: User_Info
       Name: Alice
       Age: 30
   ```

---

4. **Graph Databases:**
   - Use nodes, edges, and properties to represent and store data.
   - Best for managing relationships and connections.
   - Example: **Neo4j, Amazon Neptune**
   - Use Case: Social networks, fraud detection, recommendation engines.

   **Example Graph:**
   ```
   Node: Alice
   Relationship: FOLLOWS
   Node: Bob
   ```

---

### **Advantages of NoSQL**

1. **Scalability:**
   - Easily scale horizontally to accommodate large datasets.
2. **Flexibility:**
   - Can store diverse types of data, including hierarchical or nested data.
3. **Performance:**
   - Optimized for read/write operations, especially in high-traffic systems.
4. **Distributed Nature:**
   - Built for distributed environments, ensuring high availability.
5. **Cost-Effective:**
   - Open-source options available and often require less hardware for scaling.

---

### **Disadvantages of NoSQL**

1. **Lack of Standardization:**
   - No standard query language like SQL; each NoSQL database has its syntax.
2. **Consistency Trade-offs:**
   - Many NoSQL databases prioritize availability over consistency (CAP theorem).
3. **Complexity:**
   - May require more work for complex queries compared to SQL.
4. **Limited Maturity:**
   - Some NoSQL databases are newer and may lack the maturity of relational systems.

---

### **When to Use NoSQL**
- **High Scalability Needs:**
   - Applications with high data volumes or rapidly growing datasets.
- **Flexible Schema Requirements:**
   - When your data structure changes frequently.
- **Real-Time Analytics:**
   - For analyzing massive amounts of data quickly.
- **Unstructured or Semi-Structured Data:**
   - Logs, IoT data, social media data, or hierarchical data.
- **High Availability and Fault Tolerance:**
   - For distributed systems that cannot afford downtime.

---

### **Popular NoSQL Databases and Use Cases**

| **Database**    | **Type**         | **Best Use Cases**                      |
|------------------|------------------|-----------------------------------------|
| MongoDB          | Document Store   | E-commerce, CMS, IoT data               |
| Cassandra        | Column Store     | Time-series data, large-scale analytics |
| Redis            | Key-Value Store  | Caching, real-time leaderboards         |
| Neo4j            | Graph Database   | Social networks, fraud detection        |
| DynamoDB         | Key-Value Store  | Serverless applications, IoT            |
| Couchbase        | Document Store   | Session storage, mobile apps            |

---

### **Key Differences: NoSQL vs. SQL**

| **Aspect**          | **SQL**                      | **NoSQL**                     |
|----------------------|------------------------------|--------------------------------|
| **Data Model**       | Relational (tables)          | Flexible (key-value, graph)   |
| **Schema**           | Fixed schema                | Schema-less or dynamic        |
| **Scalability**      | Vertical (scale up)          | Horizontal (scale out)        |
| **Query Language**   | SQL (standardized)           | Varies (MongoDB, CQL, etc.)   |
| **Consistency**      | Strong (ACID transactions)   | Often eventual (BASE model)   |
| **Best For**         | Structured data, OLTP        | Big data, real-time analytics |

---

### **CAP Theorem in NoSQL**
The CAP theorem states that a distributed database can guarantee at most two of the following three properties:
1. **Consistency (C):** Every read gets the most recent write.
2. **Availability (A):** Every request gets a response (success/failure).
3. **Partition Tolerance (P):** The system continues to operate even if the network is partitioned.

- NoSQL databases often prioritize **Availability** and **Partition Tolerance** over strict **Consistency**.

---

### **NoSQL Query Examples**

#### **1. MongoDB Query**
```javascript
// Find all students with marks greater than 80
db.Students.find({ marks: { $gt: 80 } });
```

#### **2. Cassandra Query**
```sql
-- Select all rows from a table
SELECT * FROM students WHERE department_id = 101;
```

#### **3. Redis Command**
```bash
SET user:1 "Alice"
GET user:1
```

#### **4. Neo4j Query (Cypher)**
```cypher
MATCH (a:Person)-[:FOLLOWS]->(b:Person)
WHERE a.name = 'Alice'
RETURN b.name;
```

---

### **Conclusion**
NoSQL databases are powerful tools for handling modern application demands like scalability, flexibility, and real-time processing. While they are not a replacement for relational databases, they complement them in scenarios where relational models struggle. Choosing the right database depends on your application’s specific requirements.

$servername = "localhost";
$username = "root";
$password = "root";
$dbname = "colleges";

// Create connection
$conn = mysqli_connect($servername, $username, $password, $dbname);
// Check connection
if (!$conn) {
  die("Connection failed: " . mysqli_connect_error());
}

$sql = "INSERT INTO Guest (firstname, lastname, email)
VALUES ('John', 'Doe', 'john@example.com')";

if (mysqli_query($conn, $sql)) {
  echo "New record created successfully";
} else {
  echo "Error: " . $sql . "<br>" . mysqli_error($conn);
}

mysqli_close($conn);
?>
